Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 114

— Hai Ke

Editor-in-chief (to a reporter): In your news稿, you said that three thousand nine hundred and ninety-nine eyes were focused on the chairman. Why do you remember such a stupid number?

Reporter: Because you often say that accuracy is the most important thing in reporting, so I remember it especially accurately. There were indeed that many eyes.

Editor-in-chief: But why not say four thousand, and insist on coming up with a fractional number?

Reporter: Because one of them was blind in one eye.

Gardener (pointing to a tobacco plant and saying to a little girl): This is the best tobacco from abroad. It will bloom soon.

Little girl: Then when will it bear cigarettes and cigars after it blooms?

Father: Child, why don't you study geography properly? When I ask you about place names, you can't answer nine out of ten.

Son: Father, I heard the teacher say that the world map is changing every year, so I want to wait until it's a little stable in a few years before I study it.

Lawyer (having lost his coat in the courtroom cloakroom, questioning the judge): How can there be theft in a solemn courtroom?

Judge: Why make a fuss about losing a coat? My clothes are often lost in whole sets.

A Brief Account of Miao Customs in Guizhou Province 115

— Fang Zilian, sent from Majiang County, Guizhou Province

The Museum of the Academia Sinica recently organized a natural science survey team for Guizhou. It departed from Beijing on April 11th, entered Guizhou via Chongqing, Sichuan. After arriving in Guizhou, the team investigated the distribution of flora and fauna in counties such as Tongzi, Zunyi, Guiyang, Longli, Guiding, and Duyun. As a result, many flora and fauna that had not been discovered by predecessors were collected. The animal group arrived in Majiang County (formerly Maha County) on July 15th. County Magistrate Wu Gengtang and local groups hosted a banquet to welcome them. During the banquet, County Magistrate Wu described two Miao customs in the county, which were quite interesting. I hereby record them.

Miao Marriage: Every year on the 24th day of the sixth month of the lunar calendar, the Miao people in the territory gather in a village. There is a customary welcoming of gods and a race meeting. Because the Miao people's intelligence is not developed, the official government cannot prohibit it. However, in order to maintain order at the time, the police are dispatched to the scene to suppress it. On this day, no less than ten thousand people attend the meeting, with the most being young men and women. When they first arrive at the scene, they go to the gods to burn incense and kowtow, and they also murmur prayers in their mouths. Unmarried men and women pay their respects to the gods and then sing to each other on the hillside. This singing and that harmony seem to contain infinite pleasure. The sound is buzzing, but it is a pity that it cannot be discerned what song is being sung. But there are those who dance with their hands and feet, those who cover their faces in shyness, and those who lower their heads and play with their clothes. All kinds of shapes and colors are extremely laughable. If men and women sing to agree, they can ask each other about their families. After returning home, they can also arrange to meet. Parents know but do not stop them. However, the meeting place must not be known to the woman's older sister, otherwise both parties will suffer. After several meetings, if both parties think that they are in love, they will exchange ornaments. Then the man's family officially asks an intermediary to propose marriage to the woman's family. The bride price ranges from ten yuan to forty or fifty yuan, depending on the poverty or wealth of the man's family. When the wedding date arrives, the intermediary leads the bride to the husband's house for the wedding ceremony. However, the bride returns to her mother's house on the same day. She must wait until after childbirth before returning to the husband's house with the child to live together. Otherwise, she will still live in her mother's house for ten or five years, and the husband's family cannot intervene.

Avoid Calling Someone "Oldest": In Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and other places, people respectfully call others "Oldest." However, the Miao people are not like that. Because the firstborn child of the Miao people is not born to the biological father. Therefore, if we politely call a Miao person "Oldest," they will think it is a major insult. Travelers in Guizhou should pay attention to this. (Compensation)

Treatment for Acute Dysentery 116

— Zhizhi Jushi

Recently, I saw in Free Talk that Mrs. Huang Yuzhai suffered from acute dysentery and died in two days. My friend Li Kefang also suffered from this disease and died in four days. At the beginning, both had abdominal pain. In the case of Mr. Li, on the second day, he had shortness of breath and vomiting, and his upper body felt cold. By the third day, although the pain had stopped, he had explosive diarrhea, which was still incurable. Dysentery was called Zhixia in ancient times. If it is mistakenly regarded as diarrhea and treated with astringent methods, it will not be effective and will hasten death. Whether it is old or young, or dysentery after illness, it should be treated by clearing and not by astringency. The theory of Liu Hejian, a great master of the Yuan Dynasty, is the most accurate. He said: "It is a fallacy to say that red is hot and white is cold. This is caused by the accumulation of summer heat, dampness, wind, and cold. It will not work if it is not cleared." Knowing that acute abdominal pain must have more accumulation than chronic pain. The best prescription is Wang Haogu's Peony Decoction from the Yuan Dynasty. The prescription is: raw white peony two qian, betel nut one qian, wine-fried rhubarb two qian, raw licorice eight fen. The beauty lies in the wine-fried rhubarb. Cold and cold are both suitable. Although rhubarb is cold, wine is warm. Peony harmonizes the abdominal pain, betel nut breaks it, and licorice harmonizes it. The task is completed. With this prescription, this disease need not be feared to be incurable.

Three Wonders of Suzhou 117

— Dao Di

Yesterday, Mr. Li Meichu and I visited the Villa of Emerald Bamboo belonging to Mr. Zhuang in Suzhou, with ten thousand pieces of bamboo and greenery all around, an excellent place to escape the summer heat. Mr. Li will be going to the islands of Southeast Asia for a commercial survey and will be leaving in a week. Guest Zhou Zi, a relative of Mr. Zhuang, is skilled in poetry and painting and lives in Yong. He has just returned from a tour of Suzhou and said that there are very few places to visit in Suzhou, and even the Lingering Garden outside the city is very ordinary. Shantang and Tiger Hill only have a few historical sites and are not particularly wonderful. I said to Mr. Zhou, "Suzhou has three wonders. Have you ever visited them?" He asked, "What are the three wonders?" I said, "These three wonders are often praised by Qu Shi Li Yinquan, a cabinet scholar. One is the Ruiyun Peak in the old Weaving Bureau, a strange stone. It is now owned by the secondary school of the private Zhenhua Girls' School. The magnificence of this stone is almost comparable to the Zheyun admired by Zha Yihuang. The old Weaving Bureau was formerly the garden of Zhou, the maternal uncle of Emperor Chongzhen of the Ming Dynasty. In addition to this towering giant stone, there are many strange stones around it, known as the Hundred Birds Paying Homage to the Phoenix, with the many stones representing the hundred birds and the Ruiyun Peak representing the phoenix. Another is the Wisteria planted by Wen Zhengming. Its roots are larger than a basket. It is supported by wooden pillars. In the spring and summer, flowers and leaves are luxuriant, and the courtyard is full of shade. Viewers are amazed that they have never seen it before. The other is the rockery of Wang's Huan Cui Villa. It was made by Ni Yunlin after stacking the Lion Grove rockery with the remaining stones. The structure is extremely strange. It occupies a small area, but it spirals up from the foot of the mountain into the cave to reach the top of the mountain. The road is very winding, with a sense of endless layers. What is seen elsewhere cannot be compared. Having come to Suzhou, these three wonders must be visited." Mr. Zhou sighed, "I missed it this time. I will definitely visit it specially in the future." A gentleman at the table said, "Lion Grove has long enjoyed a great reputation. Why can't it be compared with these three wonders?" I said, "There is a reason for this. It is not just the private opinion of Li Yan Kui. Since Lion Grove was bought by a certain family, they have made great changes, moving the original stones at will, and the achievements of Ni Gaoshi's design and management no longer exist. I heard that a certain celebrity has a poem mocking it, saying, 'It is a pity that the painting of Ni Zan has been exchanged for a book on the cargo trade of Longmen.' These fourteen words cover it all." Mr. Li said, "Indeed. I went to West Lake last month and believed that people say that the current Xizi is not wrong in wearing a suit." Then they laughed together.

Bamboo Leaf Shoes 118

— Xu Xiaoting

The bamboo forest is shaded, the green leaves are shaking, the air is fresh, and the sun is shielded. In the past, those who traveled on dry roads, passing under the bamboo forest, loved to pick three or five tender leaves and pad them under their shoes to cool their toes and walk lightly, which was convenient for walking. There was a wealthy gentleman in Jiangbei, Gu, who had many concubines. There was a bamboo garden in his house. In the summer, the concubines cooled off in it, competing in gorgeous evening dresses. Light gauze was as thin as cicada wings. These women all liked to wear slippers, taking them to be cool and convenient. There was a Wu concubine who was twenty-nine years old and had a very clever nature. The other day, she invited her companions to pick bamboo leaves in the cool evening, filling a basket. (When picking, they took the ones with large leaves and green color to use. After picking, each leaf was split into several pieces, and then they began to weave a kind of fabric. Those who saw it all praised it. The next day, suddenly saw that the concubine made a pair of slippers, completely woven of bamboo leaves. The color was as blue as washing, and the green was dripping. At that time, a certain concubine proposed, "On the shoes, it is appropriate to attach bright pearls and embroider ocher petals to match the color." The proposal was approved. Everyone joined in a large-scale work. Wu promised. Some helped to embroider flowers, and some helped to pick leaves. Wu wove all day long. In a few days, each concubine had a pair. When wearing, they were a hundred times cooler than ordinary slippers. Moreover, the green shoes were embellished with a touch of ocher flowers and a few bright pearls, making them more gorgeous and lovely. From then on, the round six-inch feet had something to rely on. In the laughter, they all boasted that the bamboo leaf shoes were comfortable to wear, a hundred times more valuable than the slippers sold on the market.

A Short History of the British in Shanghai (1) 119

— Zhen

The Shanghai North-China Herald held its 80th anniversary of publication on August 3rd. Its commemorative volume contains a short history of the British in Shanghai. Although there are many self-praising words in it, it has reference value for the development of Shanghai. I hereby translate it directly for the public to read.

The history of the British in Shanghai is the history of Shanghai. The British Navy did not receive the help of other countries in seizing the mouth of Wusong and advancing to the public concession area, crossing the Old Zha Bridge. At the same time, the British warships destroyed the Chinese Huangpu Battery. According to the Huangpu Battery, which is now the site of the British Consulate. The British army later went to Nanjing, and the Treaty of Nanjing and its appendices were signed in 1842 and 1843 respectively. These treaties stipulated the opening of Shanghai and four other places as trading ports. This was the beginning of extraterritoriality and the treaty port system.

Britain took the lead, bearing the brunt of the war, paying the war expenses, and setting a precedent. Other countries followed suit. When the smoke of the British guns cleared all obstacles in 1844, the people of other countries lived peacefully in the trading ports of Shanghai without firing a shot and enjoyed all special rights. The Shanghai concession was originally a ceded land owned by the British for twenty years. Then the French established another organization that suited their own needs. On the other hand, the British concession merged with the American concession on the north bank of the Suzhou River to form a public concession.

The first British consul in Shanghai was Colonel Balfour. The staff included translator Medhurst, doctor Hale, and secretary Stratham. Consul Balfour arrived in Shanghai on November 8, 1843. Six days later, he rented a Gu family house with a total of fifty-two rooms on Sanyao Road in Shanghai city and established the consulate there. At that time, other British people who came to Shanghai included Dr. Lockhart and his wife, and the sister of Sir Parker. She was the first Western woman to set foot in Shanghai and died in 1918 at the age of ninety-two. In December of the same year (referring to 1843), twenty-five British people were registered at the consulate, including Wise of Jardine Matheson & Co., Gibb of Dent & Co., Smith of Dent & Co., Beale, and Dalgleish of Jardine Matheson & Co. The first to formally lease land and build houses. The first map (referring to the land deed of the British Consulate) was for Jardine Matheson & Co. The third map was for Dent & Co. The fourth map was for Wise & Co. The fifth map was for Wu Kaut and Betts. The eighth and ninth maps were for Dent & Co. (Note: Wu Kaut was a British man and was the first British Consul in Shanghai)

In the first six weeks after Shanghai opened as a trading port, seven ships entered the Mansang warehouse. The largest was named Elizabeth Wal, with a weight of 423 tons. The smallest was named Guanreba, weighing 171 tons. The average tonnage of the seven ships was 281 tons. The value of imported goods was 433,720 yuan. The value of exports was 146,072 yuan. In addition to those who formally leased land and built houses, there were many other foreign businessmen, including British people, who gathered along the river outside Shanghai County, which is now the Nanshi. Many missionaries lived in the city. Initially, foreigners did not use the concession much as a place for business. It was not until the British Consulate moved from the city to its current location on July 21, 1849, that it changed greatly.

Warmth in the Heart (257) 120

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 13 Who Plants Fortune Unintentionally Gets Diamond Ring Only This Fate Has The Intention To Sing Golden Threads

Speaking of the family of Yi Yuanyuan, it can be regarded as a story of a Shanghai prostitute family. It turns out that Yi Yuanyuan's father was a cook, and he was also a master. In addition to contracting banquets for several wealthy merchants in Shanghai, he also opened a meal-wrapping business, which also had some savings. Unexpectedly, this Chef Chen was not only good at cooking, but also an engineer at a brick and tile company. He had two wives and a total of thirteen daughters. The ancients said that giving birth to a daughter was called playing with tiles. His two wives were all tile kilns. He was really a good brick and tile master. Although he was a cook, he had great ambitions. With some money, he wanted to expand his business. So he opened a restaurant. Everything in Shanghai was expensive, and all kinds of equipment had to be complete. Even a restaurant was not a small capital to run. Only the rent in Shanghai scared the people in the inland. All kinds of food stores had to blow the conch sufficiently and also had to be a little slippery. On the one hand, they properly asked someone to help them. Chef Chen was an honest man and opened an honest shop. In less than two years, he had almost exhausted all his savings and also lost several thousand yuan. He lost money opening a restaurant. The idea turned to the brick and tile company. At that time, his eldest daughter was already in the flower-like age, and the younger one was still in swaddling clothes. In the past, the person in charge of the restaurant business was very close to the brothels. For example, brothels used to install telephones without the brothels being named, but mostly with the restaurants being named as evidence. Chef Chen wanted to do business in the Tangzi, so his restaurant was also opened in the area where Qu Yuan gathered. Therefore, his several daughters were inevitably influenced by what they saw and heard and gradually became associated with gorgeous clothes and makeup and saw that although he was a cook, the daughters he gave birth to were all dressed in powder and jade and grew up with natural beauty and unusual romance, and one was better than the other, and the younger ones were more beautiful. The seventh was better than the sixth, and the ninth was more beautiful than the eighth. Counting to Yi Yuanyuan, she was already ranked tenth and was a talent who surpassed the sisters. The ancients said that slow hiding taught theft and slow color taught lasciviousness. With so many beautiful daughters, people said that Chef Chen had not gone bankrupt, even if one daughter was called a thousand gold, he had thirteen daughters, which was equivalent to thirteen thousand gold. So many people encouraged him to open a Tangzi, and some people arranged marriages for the older daughters, promising them to be concubines. In this way, not only were the debts cleared, but also several thousand yuan were added. Helplessly, his heart for opening a restaurant never died. The second time he opened a restaurant, the scale of the second restaurant was larger than the first time. It was another loss. He still had to find a way on several daughters. This Chef Chen really carried out the sentence of Wuxi scholar Wu Zhihui, the elder of the party and the country, saying that the mouth was wide and the debt was tight.

Financial Gold Crashes by Twenty Taels 121

Selling Storm is Irresistible, Bullish Spirit Disappears

Those Who Get Out Rush Out. Yesterday, the 18th, the situation of the gold market was unusually weak, with a sharp decline of as much as twenty taels, which was caused by the large bullish accounts selling off one after another. There were twists and turns of more than eleven taels before and after the market, rising and falling suddenly. In a short period of time, there were two or three taels to five or six taels of fluctuations, and the market situation was deeply bizarre, with people being extremely panic-stricken. The storm was raging, and the bullish arrogance had been extinguished. As for the foreign exchange, it also declined. The market was still relatively busy, but the supply was always greater than the demand. Hengxingsheng, Dachengfeng, Yongxing and other treasures encouraged the market, while Yuanxing, Yongyifeng, Yongxing and others bought in. Weakness of Foreign Exchange 122

Observations on US Cotton Trends 127

Production of 14 Million Bales is Sufficient for Consumption and More

This year's US cotton market has been weak due to the global cotton industry's decline, hovering between 0.15 and 0.16. Between March and June, the cooperative's price maintenance measures failed, and the market price quickly fell to 0.13. Subsequently, the government's new cotton estimate was only 27% lower than the previous season, making it impossible to reverse the declining market trend. Although the drought affected fertility, the poor trade in cotton goods and the government's cotton production report, along with ample supply, failed to attract buyers. Furthermore, the sharp reduction in sales and the disappearance of insect pests caused the market price to drop sharply again, breaking through the 0.12 mark, the lowest price since the 1926 bumper harvest. The future trend will depend on the production and consumption of new cotton.

The government's first cotton field estimate for this season is 45,815,000 acres, a decrease of 5.5% compared to the same period last year, a decrease of only 2.7% compared to the revised figure, a decrease of 24% compared to 1927, and a decrease of 6% compared to 1926. This estimate includes fields abandoned after planting due to special reasons. The difference between the first estimate and the revised acreage is the abandoned acreage. The amount of abandoned acreage this season is unknown, but based on the average of 3.5% for abandoned acreage between 1920 and 1929, the estimated harvested cotton acreage this year is about 44,211,000 acres. A comparison of cotton fields in various states and the average rate of abandoned acreage over ten years is listed above (unit: thousands of acres).

State: This Season, Last Season, Increase/Decrease, Percentage, 1920-1929 Average Cotton Field Abandonment Percentage

Virginia: 90, 89, 1, 0.120

North Carolina: 1724, 1916, -192, 0.016

South Carolina: 2205, 2273, -68, 0.027

Georgia: 3818, 3818, 0, 0.036

Florida: 106, 96, 10, 0.056

Mississippi: 3833, 4711, -878, 0.048

Other States: 19, 19, 0, 0.046

Total: 45825, 47067, -1242, 0.035

The number of harvests is difficult to predict due to changes in the weather and the state of insect pests. Based on the harvested cotton acreage of 44,311,000 acres this year, the harvest is estimated to be about 13,652,000 bales based on the average harvest of 154.4 pounds per acre in the last ten years. Based on the average harvest of 163 pounds per acre in the last five years, the harvest is about 14,413,000 bales. The average production is about 14 million bales. In addition to reports of drought this year, losses from insect pests have been avoided. If there are no special circumstances in the future, a harvest of 13,652,000 bales can be regarded as the low end of cotton production this season. If the drought-stricken areas can get rain early and have suitable weather, the harvest of 14,413,000 bales can be expected.

Although a harvest of 14 million bales cannot be considered a bumper harvest, it can be regarded as an oversupply in the current trend of the global cotton industry's decline. Based on the current situation, it is impossible for the US cotton consumption this year to reach 14 million bales. The number of year-end inventories is likely to increase, approaching or even exceeding the 7,338,000 bales in 1927. Even if the global cotton industry can gradually turn around, the supply of over 14 million bales is sufficient, and the inventory of 6,340,000 bales cannot be eliminated. The trend of the cotton market will be difficult to recover for a while and will hover at a low peak (August 16).

Jin Li Yuan Wharf Case 149

Yesterday, the negotiation reached a satisfactory conclusion. The judicial authorities were prevented from executing the order, the lease agreement was maintained, and arbitration was initiated immediately.

Yesterday afternoon at 4 o'clock, Cai Pei, the director of the China Merchants Bureau, together with Liu Yunfang, the deputy director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office, and Gao Shuo, the legal advisor of the bureau, went to the French Consulate to meet with the French Consul-General Ganggelin to discuss and resolve the Jin Li Yuan Wharf dispute. The talks between the two sides lasted about an hour, and a very satisfactory result was achieved. The French Consul has made a clear statement regarding the resolution of this case. The main points of the discussion between the two sides are recorded separately below:

Director Cai's Statement: I am very grateful to Your Consul-General for sincerely mediating this matter based on diplomatic relations. However, the approximate key points of this case that should be clarified are: (1) The land evidence filled in by the Bureau (official document from Shanghai County to the Ministry of Revenue on February 6th of the Guangxu era requesting the issuance of a license). (2) Shanghai Daotai Gong Zhaoyu's correspondence with the French Consul-General De stating that the land must be leased to the China Merchants Bureau (Shanghai Daotai's letter to the French Consul on August 29th of the Guangxu era). (3) The French Consul-General De's reply to the Shanghai Daotai stating that the original land would be leased to the China Merchants Bureau for use (letter from the French Consul to the Shanghai Daotai on January 19th of the Guangxu era). (4) When issuing the deed to Sandetang, a condition was attached that the French Consul should order it to be leased to the China Merchants Bureau for use as currently discussed (official document from the Shanghai Daotai to the China Merchants Bureau on December 20th of the Guangxu era). (5) Clause 11 of the contract signed by both parties on December 4th, 1916 states that if there is any dispute regarding the interpretation and implementation of this contract, it should be submitted to arbitration. Sandetang's rash lawsuit this time violates the provisions of the contract. (6) Restriction on land price: Clause 2 of the original contract states that the valuation during the first 25 years of this lease shall not exceed 300,000 taels, and shall not exceed 350,000 taels during the subsequent 25 years, but in any case, it shall not be lower than 240,000 taels. Our Bureau will consider the reason and situation and will never let them suffer losses. The number can be arbitrated by the arbitrator, but it must be bound by the original contract. Our Bureau has also appointed lawyer Gao Shuo as the arbitrator for this matter. Please inform Sandetang to start the arbitration immediately and ask Your Consul to express your opinion.

The French Consul's Statement: Director Liu has repeatedly explained the points raised by Director Cai to the French Consul and marked them down. According to the French Consul's reply, according to Article 10 of the contract, if the rent is in arrears, the lease can be canceled, but it does not state that the China Merchants Bureau will not be able to enjoy the Jin Li Yuan Wharf after the lease is canceled. These are two completely different matters. Because Sandetang is purely a church organization, the only purpose of its priests renting land is to obtain rent on time. If there is an arrear, the contract can be cancelled. As for what your bureau claims, according to the lease regulations, if there is any dispute, it can be submitted to arbitration. Sandetang has now prepared arbitrators, but the China Merchants Bureau has not yet appointed arbitrators to negotiate with Sandetang, which has led to legal proceedings. Now that the Director of the China Merchants Bureau has agreed to appoint arbitrators to negotiate with the representatives of Sandetang to resolve all problems, the legal aspect will naturally not be a problem. The French Consul-General also said that regarding the execution of the cancellation of the lease by the French Public Concession Court, the original hearing was scheduled to continue on Tuesday (i.e., today). Whether to execute it, this Consul-General will be responsible for delaying the execution of the judgment to seek a peaceful solution and will be responsible for notifying Sandetang to prepare to open negotiations with the China Merchants Bureau to resolve the dispute. As for what your Director said, the only purpose now is to continue to maintain the lease between the two parties and appropriately increase the annual rent. This Consul-General can guarantee that it can be handled accordingly. But there is one point that needs to be stated urgently, that is, regarding what your Director said, the annual rent can be increased appropriately, but it cannot be increased beyond the contract. This Consul-General can reply on behalf of the priests that it can always be discussed. However, ensuring that the annual rent is paid on time is the most important key. A practical guarantee should be given by the arbitrator of the China Merchants Bureau and the arbitrator of Sandetang. Please note that the French Consul-General finally stated that the negotiations this afternoon have made great progress and are gratifying. Director Cai and others stated that the negotiation results were satisfactory, and they shook hands and said goodbye.

Meeting of the French Municipal Council Yesterday afternoon at half past five, the board of directors of the French Municipal Council held a meeting. Chinese directors Zhang Xiaolin, Du Yuehe, and Huang Jinrong all attended. During the meeting, all the directors requested French Consul-General Ke Ge Lin to report on the results of the meeting with Cai Pei, the director of the China Merchants Bureau. The French Consul reported in detail. All the directors expressed their satisfaction with the French Consul's measures to prevent the execution by the French Public Concession Court and to initiate arbitration. The meeting adjourned at about seven o'clock.

Director Cai's Remarks: Director Cai told reporters that the reason why he came to Shanghai twice from Beijing to assume the responsibility of acting as the director of the Bureau was that he deeply understood that the China Merchants Bureau's lawsuit in the Sandetang lease dispute had failed. Only six days remained before the cancellation of the lease would be executed when he came to Shanghai to continue acting as the director. If the China Merchants Bureau's Jin Li Yuan Wharf was divided and suffered a significant loss in property value, and if it was impossible to connect the wharves, it would be greatly related to sovereignty. Therefore, he resolutely came back because the situation was urgent and allowed no delay. He relied heavily on Gao Shuo in handling this matter. Now he has stated to the French Consul that the original contract will still be leased to the China Merchants Bureau for continued use, but considering the current land price, the rent should also be increased appropriately. The result of the negotiation with the French Consul this time is to fundamentally revoke the two lawsuits (because the third appeal must be made to Paris). It is only possible to abandon the law and speak of the facts. Under the restrictions of the contract, each party will appoint arbitrators to appropriately increase the rent. This matter will be implemented soon. In this wharf lease dispute case, the Bureau can still be considered to have prevailed. The reporter also asked whether the new director Chen Xizeng will come to take over immediately. Cai said that the clear order has been seen and he can certainly come to take over.

Chen Xizeng, the new director of the China Merchants Bureau, has formally received an order from the National Government and is scheduled to go to Nanjing today to contact various parties regarding the funding issues of the China Merchants Bureau. Total Revenue of the Municipal Council in the First Half of This Year 152

Six Million Sixty-Nine Thousand One Hundred and Seventeen Taels

The North China Daily News says that the progressive development of the Public Concession can be seen in the number of revenues released by the Municipal Council. The total revenue for the first half of this year was 6,069,117 taels, while the same period last year was only 5,703,167 taels. Although there was 6,830,552 taels in the year before last, there was a payment of 1.5 million taels for electrical contracts, which is still less than last year and this year after deducting this item. Among them, the largest increase was in patrol fees. In the first half of this year, Westerners paid a total of 1,329,019 taels, compared to 1,200,894 taels last year and only 1,107,441 taels the year before last. Westerners paid a total of 151,345 taels in special fees, compared to only 142,059 taels last year. Chinese paid a total of 1,583,796 taels in patrol fees, compared to 1,478,347 taels in the same period last year. However, the number of Chinese special fees was slightly reduced because some Chinese residences on both sides of the cross-border roads have been changed to pay total fees to the municipal finance bureau. In total, the patrol fee item increased by more than 242,000 taels in the first half of this year compared to the same period last year. However, given the recent prosperity of construction in the concession, this increase is not surprising. In addition, land tax increased by more than 14,000 taels. Fees for foreign theaters and Chinese theaters each increased by 1,000 taels. Other entertainment venues also jumped from 4,993 taels to 7,049 taels. The registration fee for brothels even increased from 31,047 taels to 34,037 taels. However, the registration fee for hotels decreased from 23,271 taels to 21,918 taels, and the registration fee for foreign liquor stores also decreased by 450 taels, indicating the depression of the two industries. On the contrary, the pawn industry is thriving, and its registration fee has increased from 27,103 taels to 35,483 taels, resulting in an increase of more than 8,000 taels in municipal revenue. From these two points, we can see the decline of people's livelihood and the increase of the poor. The income from the registration fees of tobacco shops, small money shops, silver buildings, lighters, and small boats is similar to that of last year. As for transportation tools, the registration fees for automobiles and automobile rooms increased by more than 50,000 taels. Although there are many freight cars, the number of taxis has not only not decreased but also increased. The registration fee also increased by 2,439 taels in the first half of the year. The registration fee for private chartered cars increased by more than 5,000 taels, and the number of rickshaws also increased by several hundred, while the number of small carts slightly decreased. In addition, wharf fees have always been a major source of income, and they have increased year by year. The first half of 1928 was 269,545 taels, last year was

Summary of Commemorative Weeks at Various Institutions 155

The Municipal Executive Committee held its 16th weekly Sun Yat-sen Memorial yesterday. All executive and supervisory committee members and staff attended and performed the rituals as usual. Standing Committee member Wu Bokang presided over the meeting and reported on the work of the various departments and committees in the past week, followed by a concise report on Party affairs and political matters. The meeting then adjourned.

The Municipal Government held its weekly Sun Yat-sen Memorial yesterday. The Secretary-General, councilors, secretaries, section chiefs, and all staff members attended. The Secretary-General presided over the meeting and conducted the rituals as usual. First, Assistant Secretary Chen Kecheng reported on the domestic political situation of the past week. Then, the Secretary-General reported on the progress of municipal administration in the past week. The ceremony concluded and the meeting adjourned at around 10:00 AM.

The Bureau held its 100th weekly Sun Yat-sen Memorial yesterday. Over one hundred people attended, including the section chiefs and all staff members. Director Pan, the Bureau Chief, presided over the meeting and conducted the rituals as usual. The Director reported on the recent domestic political and military situation. The ceremony concluded and the meeting adjourned at around 5:00 PM.

The Naval Special District Party Headquarters held a combined weekly Sun Yat-sen Memorial and commemorative service for Mr. Liao Zhongkai yesterday. The Naval Special District Party Headquarters, together with the Naval Compilation and Legacy Office, convened representatives from various ships and organizations for a ceremony in the department's main hall. Over one hundred people attended. Zheng Youyi presided over the meeting, and Cai Linbing gave a political report. The chairman then described Mr. Liao's revolutionary history, the circumstances of his martyrdom, and the efforts we should make in his memory. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 AM.

The Two-Roads Party Headquarters held its 57th weekly Sun Yat-sen Memorial yesterday. Standing Committee member Min presided over the meeting, leading everyone in the rituals as usual. Afterward, he reported on the political situation of the past week. After the report, Committee member Chen, the director of the organization section, exhorted the comrades to take on their responsibilities. The ceremony concluded and the meeting adjourned.

The Shanghai County Government held its weekly memorial yesterday. Secretary Ye Dezhen presided over the meeting and conducted the rituals as usual. Afterward, the chairman reported that County Magistrate Yan had been ordered by the provincial government to go to Qingpu County today to supervise an oath-taking ceremony and could not attend the memorial. The representative of brothers presided and reported on the internal affairs of the past week. Then, various bureaus reported in succession. The ceremony concluded and the meeting adjourned.

The Arsenal held its weekly memorial at 11:00 AM yesterday. Director of General Affairs Xu Mujun presided over the meeting and conducted the rituals as usual. Kuang Yunwen, an officer of the factory's Party Ideology Research Association, reported on political and military affairs. The ceremony concluded at 12:00 PM.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce held its weekly Sun Yat-sen Memorial yesterday. Standing Committee member Yuan Ludeng presided over the meeting and conducted the rituals as usual. The chairman gave a brief report, followed by Secretary-General Zheng Chengqing, who reported on important domestic and international commercial matters of the past week. Next, staff members took turns giving speeches on Party ideology.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Discusses Developing Trade with India 156

Meeting to Be Held Tomorrow

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, in order to discuss methods for promoting domestic goods in India, has scheduled a meeting to be held tomorrow (the 20th) at 4:00 PM. The text of its telegram and notice are recorded below:

Telegram to the Consul-General in India: To the Chinese Consulate-General in Calcutta, regarding the instruction from the Ministry that the Indian people's boycott of British goods presents a favorable opportunity for our country to develop foreign trade, please secretly submit three methods for consideration. This matter is of utmost importance, and we instruct you to forward it to all relevant businesses for their information. At the same time, we have received a request from the Indian S. Mela to negotiate methods for promoting foreign trade and he is willing to take on the responsibility of publicity. This matter concerns the development of foreign trade. In addition to convening representatives from domestic goods merchants and factories in this city to discuss implementation, we must first investigate the import tax rates and needed commodities of India to facilitate planning. We hereby telegram you, Consul-General, requesting that you promptly investigate and reply to allow us to begin handling this matter. Utmost urgency. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Xian Yin.

Letter to Relevant Businesses: To the relevant businesses, we hereby notify you that we have received an instruction from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, stating that it has approved a confidential report from the Consulate-General in Calcutta that the Indian people are fervently boycotting British goods, which presents a good opportunity for our national goods to develop foreign trade. We have been instructed to notify all businesses for their information. At the same time, we have received a request from the Indian S. Mela to negotiate methods for promoting domestic goods, which is a matter of utmost importance. Issue of Bank Rice Mortgage Loans 159

Bank Association Claims Not to Have Provided Them; Money Shops Association Yet to Respond

The Social Affairs Bureau previously received reports that various banks and money shops in the city were providing rice mortgage loans totaling 20 million yuan. At the time, the rice market was tense, and there was concern that unscrupulous merchants might use this financial activity to hoard and speculate. The Bureau sent separate letters to the Bank and Money Shops Associations, asking them to investigate the loan situation and amounts undertaken by their member banks and money shops, as well as the locations where the rice was stored, in order to investigate and request that future loans be made for short terms and not be allowed to be rolled over, in order to remedy the situation. A month has passed, and the Money Shops Association has not yet responded. However, the Bank Association replied that, according to the responses from the various banks, they have not undertaken any rice mortgage loans. However, there are rumors that many rice mortgage loans are supporting hoarders. It is unknown whether the banks' responses are accurate.

City Social Affairs Bureau to Burn Rice Stem Borer Eggs and Moths Today 160

Page 14

Over 800,000 Egg Masses and Over 40,000 Moths; City Could Increase Rice Harvest by Over 4,000 Dan

In view of the increasing damage caused by rice stem borers in recent years, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, in order to encourage farmers to search and capture them, applied to the Municipal Government for an appropriation to purchase them at five locations: Yinhang, Jiangwan, Wusong, Caojing, and the Pudong Municipal Agricultural Experiment Field. The situation regarding these purchases was reported in the previous issue. It is now heard that from July 1st to the 16th of this month, the Bureau has received over 800,000 rice stem borer egg masses and over 40,000 rice stem borer moths. It is said that each egg mass averages over one hundred worms, which can harm over one hundred rice plants. Each plant can produce one hundred grains of rice, so removing one egg mass can increase the grain yield by half a catty. Based on 800,000 egg masses, the city can increase its rice harvest by over 400,000 catties, or over 40 dan, equivalent to over 2,000 piculs of white rice. And the rice stem borer moths have not yet been counted. The cost is small, but the effect is great. The Bureau has determined that the rice stem borer eggs and moths are either about to hatch or have already decayed, so they will be burned today (the 19th) at 2:00 PM. The Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government have been informed and will send personnel to monitor the burning. All district municipal committee members, etc., have been ordered to attend at that time, and representatives from all sectors are expected to attend and observe.

Request to Extend Deadline for Reorganization of Trade Associations 161

Proposed Extension Until January 1931

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau states that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted that the deadline for reorganization as stipulated by the Trade Association Law is one year from the promulgation of the law. However, although the Trade Association Law was promulgated on July 17, 1929, the implementing regulations were not issued by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce until January of this year. The period for the reorganization of these associations is proposed to be calculated as one year from the issuance of the implementing regulations, extending it to January 1931. The Social Affairs Bureau has telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for instructions based on the situation.

Issue of Shop Employees Joining Trade Associations 162

New Sound Society: The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday reported that the shop employees of medicinal material stores legally joined trade associations, but were interfered with by the Medicinal Material Trade Union. They have requested the Citizens Training Committee and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to correct the situation. In addition to stating the facts, the original report also stated: "The Central Executive Committee instructed the Party Headquarters of each province on February 10 of this year that 'shop employees have also been decided by this committee to be included in the implementing regulations of the Trade Association Law, so that they have the opportunity to serve as member representatives. Once the organization is unified, the past divisions between large and small merchants, as well as disputes between shop owners and shop employees, can be fundamentally eliminated.' Therefore, the method stipulated in Article 8 of the Implementing Regulations of the Trade Association Law, which allows one additional representative for those employing more than fifteen people, is in accordance with the principles established by the Central Executive Committee. How can the trade union, under the protection of Party rule, wantonly obstruct this? As for the scope of commercial employers, Article 10 of the Implementing Regulations of the Chamber of Commerce Law clearly states that it is limited to managers, partners, and those who directly labor in the business. If students and machine operators are also serving in the business, they should also be included as commercial employers. Furthermore, Article 8 of the Implementing Regulations of the Trade Association Law revised the regulations to state that each company or firm may add one representative if it employs more than fifteen people. According to data, Tongkang Firm employs sixteen people, and the manager, representing the firm, has the right to add representatives according to law. However, the trade union forced Du Xianqing, the manager of Tongkang Firm, to admit that it was illegal. The supervisory committee does not know what laws it is based on. As for the claim that Zhang Qinzhang joined the trade association without going through legal procedures, it is also incomprehensible. According to current practice, what is formulated by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government is called law. The 'legal procedures' referred to by the trade union seem to require that commercial employers undergo a certain restriction when serving as member representatives of the trade association. This kind of restriction has not been promulgated by the National Government as a law. The 'legal procedures' referred to by the trade union should refer to some kind of restriction that the trade union has set itself. Not only can it not abuse the word 'legal,' but also, if the rules and resolutions set by the country's own body conflict with national laws, then these rules and resolutions are invalid. It is now found that when commercial employers join trade associations, there is no restriction attached to it by the laws set by the central government that they must first be approved or agreed to by the trade union. Therefore, whatever procedures the trade union sets are beyond its authority and vainly attempt to impose a kind of constraint on the central government's laws. According to the principles of law, it naturally does not take effect. If the trade union is allowed to create obstacles at will in this matter, then the instruction of the Central Executive Committee on February 10 will be fundamentally overturned. This concerns Party discipline and national credibility and is difficult to understand. The central government promulgated this decree precisely to reconcile the divisions between shop owners and shop employees, but the trade union is afraid that these divisions will be eliminated and is trying its best to create this kind of obstacle. It is impossible to guess what its intentions are, but it cannot but be considered to contain a significant meaning. According to the letter, it is reasonable to request your council to examine and verify this situation and to quickly stop the trade union's actions in accordance with the law, so that the central government's laws will not be arbitrarily destroyed by the trade union. It is difficult to express our public sentiment."

Ma Wenhuei's Discussion of the Recent Situation of Overseas Chinese in England 163

The Kuo Wen News Agency reports that Mr. Ma Wenhuei, the European manager of Sincere Company and president of the London Chinese Chamber of Commerce and former president of the British Overseas Chinese Federation, recently returned to China from England with his wife and three-year-old son, Jian Yuan, and arrived in Shanghai. Because Ma had been stationed in England for a long time and his position was extremely important, the reporter visited him at his residence to ask about the recent situation of overseas Chinese in England. Mr. Ma was humble and sincere and could speak pure Mandarin (the following are Mr. Ma's own words): "I left Shanghai for England five days before the May 30th Massacre. At that time, I knew that the situation of the massacre was very painful. After arriving in England, I tried my best to publicize the matter of the massacre and gained the sympathy of the British people for China. Later, unfortunately, the Sha Ji, Wan County, and Jinan massacres followed one after another. The overseas Chinese were moved by righteousness and generously donated money, raising a total of more than 12,000 pounds to be remitted back to the motherland to help the victims. Although this was a drop in the bucket, it could still alleviate the urgent needs. After the various massacres, a certain country focused on one-sided publicity in the newspapers. The country's publicity in foreign countries was almost impossible to talk about because there was no equivalent publicity agency to counter it. Therefore, in every international negotiation, it was difficult for the various countries to sympathize with our country. This is truly a painful thing. Even a privately organized news agency is nowhere to be found, and the government agencies' publicity is difficult to attract foreign aid. Currently, the total number of overseas Chinese in the United Kingdom is only over 2,000, including 250 students. Their economic strength has not made great progress. My long-standing aspiration has been to strive for the development of the lives and the consolidation of the status of overseas Chinese. This is not only the happiness of our overseas Chinese, but also the glory of our Party and country. Unfortunately, in recent years, the number of unemployed people in the United Kingdom has increased sharply. According to current statistics, it has reached over two million. For example, the employee vacancies in my Sincere Company must first be filled by recruiting in the United Kingdom. Only if it is impossible to do so can we recruit from China to go to the United Kingdom. Although the British Labor Department's immigration law does not prohibit overseas Chinese from entering the country, the above method has imposed an invisible restriction on overseas Chinese businessmen and workers in the United Kingdom. As for Chinese banks in the United Kingdom, there is only the Bank of China branch newly established in London. It can be called the firstborn of Chinese banks abroad and can directly do business with various manufacturers. Our country's German government bonds are completely handled by it. It is also very convenient for overseas Chinese in the United Kingdom. It has only been open for a few months, but the total business volume has reached four to five million pounds. The future is bright. It is hoped that the domestic war will end soon so as not to directly or indirectly affect foreigners' attitudes toward our China. It seems that foreigners' attitude toward China has become relatively friendly. Although both sides had resentment after the May 30th Massacre, in recent years, most British people have been able to show considerable respect to Chinese people. This is really due to the self-improvement efforts of our compatriots." Mr. Ma is the son of Mr. Ma Yingbiao, the founder of Sincere Company. This trip is to return to Guangdong Province to visit relatives. It is heard that friends in the United Kingdom still hope that he will continue to go to the United Kingdom after his holiday to seek the development of the economic lives of overseas Chinese. At the same time, the headquarters of Sincere Company in Hong Kong has also telegraphed Ma to discuss important matters. I am afraid that his whereabouts will not be easy to determine for a while. Currently, Mr. Ma is temporarily residing at Mr. Guo Shun's residence on Jing'an Temple Road, Hartong Road, in this city, lingering for a while. He plans to return to Hong Kong first in the next few days.

Japan's Trade with China Booming Last Month 164

More than Double That of June

According to statistics released yesterday by the commercial office of the Japanese Embassy, the total value of Japan's trade with China in July (i.e., the total number of Japanese goods shipped to China) was 35,900,900 yen. This number has more than doubled compared to Japan's trade with China in June, which is quite unexpected. The reason is nothing more than that the internal war in China has reduced productivity, and at the same time, the price of gold has soared, and imports of European and American goods have plummeted, so the sales of Japanese goods have become very prosperous.

Record of Yesterday's Meeting of the Families of the Xin Daming Incident 168

Discussing Japanese Compensation, the Public Endured the Pain to Acknowledge It

Three years have passed since the Xin Daming Wheel tragedy occurred. Yesterday afternoon, because the county case was not settled, the families of the victims held a special meeting to discuss whether to approve the amount of compensation offered by the Japanese side and how to distribute the compensation after it is received. At that time, more than fifty family members attended and publicly elected Chief Representative Pei Jiesan as chairman. Pei reported that since this case occurred three years ago, the families of the victims, for the sake of national rights, people's lives, and the future development of China's shipping industry, have spared no effort to sacrifice their lives, money, and spirit to fight against Japanese imperialism and capitalism. However, the difficulties of the victims' families over the past three years cannot be described in words. Fortunately, thanks to the righteous and courageous efforts of former lawyer Wu, now lawyer Wu, and assistant Jia Yaoxi, they have done their best to handle the matter and have repeatedly negotiated with the Japanese side and appealed to various circles, which have been able to promote the Japanese side's understanding. Today, they are willing to pay 25,000 yen as compensation to all the families. At that time, our side did not approve it. Now, because the price of gold has risen to about 45,000 Chinese silver dollars, it has been approved by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and other organizations. Our victim's families have been forced to endure the pain to acknowledge it. However, how should all future receipt and disposal issues be handled? Please make a public decision. At that time, representatives of each family member put forward eleven suggestions, which were submitted to a vote by the chairman one by one and passed. The resolution methods were handed over to lawyer Wu Chengyu for implementation. Everyone agreed and adjourned the meeting. Therefore, the Xin Daming tragedy is expected to be resolved soon.

Impact of the Suspension of Refining in Huashe 170

Huashe in Shaoxing is a place where silk is produced. Each year, a large amount of silk fabrics are produced and sold at home and abroad, amounting to tens of millions of dollars. The production of these silk fabrics is first woven by weaving mills and then handed over to silk merchants for procurement. They are then handed over to refining mills for dyeing and refining, and then resold to major silk merchants in Shanghai, who distribute them to various merchants for sale at home and abroad. However, because the prices of all goods have been expensive recently, the profit margin for the refining price has always been very thin, so each refining mill has often suffered losses. The Huashe Refining Industry Association previously sent representatives to Shanghai to request the Shen Qianjiang Silk Industry Association to fulfill the agreement to increase the refining price. The Shanghai merchants had already verbally agreed. Unexpectedly, the Huashe silk merchants still did not allow it, so the refining mills have all stopped operating and working. Merchants in Shanghai believe that the impact on the autumn fabrics listing is quite large and have written to merchants in Shaoxing to explain.

Buli Duo Launches the First Sound 172

Jiufu Company in this city has created a new medicine called Buli Duo, divided into two types: Pure Jing Buli Duo and Han Ji Guai Buli Duo. It is said that its main component is the essence extracted from sea turtle liver oil, called Zhaju Er. The procedure for refining Zhaju Er is very difficult. Only a small amount of Zhaju Er can be extracted from every hundred pounds of fish liver oil, so it is also extremely valuable. In order to refine Zhaju Er, the company spent more than 100,000 gold yuan to install the latest equipment to succeed. It is also equipped with guiding, invigorating, and various tonic agents to make Pure Jing Buli Duo and Han Ji Guai Buli Duo. The manufacturing method and raw materials are exactly the same as those of popular imported products on the market. The original formula for this imported product has long been published, but all domestic pharmacies that want to manufacture according to the formula lack the economic and human resources. Now, Jiufu Company has succeeded in manufacturing it regardless of the cost. This also shows the progress of China's chemical pharmaceutical industry. It is also heard that because Buli Duo has been newly launched, it has been widely used by the medical and pharmaceutical communities. The sales channels of imported products have been greatly affected. Currently, due to limited production, it has not been able to publish large-scale promotions in newspapers. It will not be widely publicized until a large amount is produced. It is heard that domestic goods organizations in this city have introduced it to the people of the country. In the future, it will add a lot of color to the future of domestic goods.

News from Various Labor Unions 176

Cotton Mill Industry: Federation of Trade Unions, Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Cotton Mill Workers' Union - Letter to the workers of Chinese cotton mills: Dear workers, cotton textiles occupy the most needed and valuable position in the world. China, as an agricultural country, is naturally the richest country in terms of raw materials for cotton textiles. Considering its production status, it should be able to meet its own needs with surplus to supplement other countries. However, examining the facts, it is contrary to the principle of production. Which compatriot is not surprised, heartbroken, and unable to understand the reason? There are many reasons for the overall failure of China's cotton mill industry. Here, we select a few major points to tell our cotton mill workers: [T13]1[/T] Tariff rights are controlled by foreigners. In the past, China's cotton textile market was quite smooth, and business was very prosperous. This was because it was still closed off, with no competition from foreign merchants. Cotton mills were only established by Chinese people, and there were no foreign cotton mills established in China. Therefore, nineteen out of ten Chinese clothing materials were taken from domestic cotton textiles, and the supply was often insufficient to meet demand. The state of its prosperous business can be known. Since the failure of diplomacy in the late Qing Dynasty and the permission of trade, foreigners have transported all kinds of woolen, silk, and cotton goods to China. Tariff rights are controlled by foreigners, and import duties are extremely low, and there are even situations of tax evasion. These goods are all made by machines, and the products are sudden, the cost is small, the tax rate is light, and the price is cheap. Our machines are undeveloped.

Competing with it urgently leads to business decline, increased unemployment, and increased social panic. Both labor and capital suffer great losses. The control of tariff rights by foreigners is indeed the greatest fatal injury to China. [T13]2[/T] Chinese labor and capital failed to cooperate. Although the positions of capitalists and workers are different, their goals of seeking business development and common interests are the same. Therefore, capitalists and workers must have a spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation to expect business development. A good boat sails in the sea and encounters storms. Safety and danger are difficult to determine. At that time, there is no distinction between the crew and passengers in the boat. The lives of the entire boat are entrusted to one boat. Therefore, the crew and passengers are in different positions, but their main purpose is to seek safety. If a boat sinks to the bottom of the water, the crew and passengers will inevitably suffer the same fate. Is there any reason why the crew is lucky and the passengers are unlucky, or the passengers are lucky and the crew is unlucky? The capitalist is compared to the passenger, and the worker is compared to the crew. It is clear that the cooperation of capital and labor is necessary. However, today's Chinese capitalists mostly pride themselves on money and power, only knowing how to demand internally and not knowing how to develop externally, leading to unfortunate incidents. Thinking of this is really heartbreaking. [T13]3[/T] Increased tax rates affect China. In recent years, internal wars have frequently occurred, droughts and floods have occurred repeatedly, the national treasury is empty, and people's livelihood is declining. Needless to say, although the government has exhausted all resources, it is still difficult to implement various constructions. Therefore, it has to increase various tax rates to make up for maintenance. At this time, the sales of our cotton textiles are stagnant and business is dying. An increase in tax rates is also difficult to avoid. Once the tax rate is increased, the cost increases accordingly, and the selling price has to be slightly increased, causing the original sales market to suffer a sudden impact. The number of capitalists who have closed down due to their inability to maintain is not small. This is truly an unfortunate event for the future of China's industry. Does the government pay attention to it? [T13]4[/T] Workers lack unity and methods of improvement. The purpose of workers organizing groups is to unite the feelings of workers, improve industry, increase production, and implement the Three People's Principles and strive for the National Revolution. There are no fewer than dozens of cotton mills in Shanghai, and there are few organizations with strong strength. It can be seen that the disunity of our cotton mill workers is a glimpse. Without the unity of workers, each goes its own way, so what is there to discuss and improve? This is indeed the biggest shortcoming and the main reason why our cotton mill industry has failed to develop. It is easy to break a single arrow, and the crowd makes a city. The ancient teachings are now abandoned by the organization of great traitors. Why should people not blame themselves deeply? This is not what our cotton mill workers want. In short, if the cotton mill industry is not revitalized one day, the national industry will not be able to develop one day. Shanghai is the largest commercial port in the country, with cotton mills and workers numbering in the hundreds of thousands. Therefore, the development of Shanghai's cotton mill industry is of great importance to the entire country. This time, under the order of the Municipal Party Committee, members were sent to organize the Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Cotton Mill Workers' Union for the great unity of the workers in this industry. Our association has complied with the order and organized it. However, the decline of our cotton mill industry and the painful groans of the workers are overwhelming. We still hope that all the workers in our cotton mill industry will unite with the benevolence of helping each other in the same boat, and under the leadership of the Party, strive for the labor movement, and use the spirit of labor-capital cooperation to improve the industry, seek our own liberation, and fight for the survival of the nation. This is what our association is eagerly looking forward to. Workers, unite together, uphold the teachings of the Prime Minister, with the spirit of great justice and selflessness, and the perseverance of unyielding efforts, promote the realization of the Three People's Principles, and raise the country to prosperity. The Party-State is fortunate, and the labor movement is fortunate. Shout our slogan: All the cotton mill workers in the city unite together, implement labor-capital cooperation, develop industry, seek our liberation, and overthrow the corrupt elements that undermine unity. To seek a way out, we must unite and implement the Three People's Principles. Long live the Chinese Kuomintang! Long live the workers' movement! Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Cotton Mill Workers' Union.

Silk Factory Industry: Federation of Trade Unions held its third preparatory meeting yesterday, publicly electing Chen Xiu Pu as chairman. Resolutions: [T13]1[/T] The standing committee members proposed that the association of the same industry decided to re-determine the method of promotion and notified each factory to implement it without obtaining the consent of the labor side beforehand. Recent Dysentery Outbreak 177

Health Bureau administers vaccinations and compiles printed materials

The Municipal Health Bureau, in view of the reports of infectious diseases sent by various hospitals after separate statistics, found that the number of dysentery cases has increased recently. It is preparing to provide free dysentery vaccinations for citizens, but because the reaction of the dysentery vaccination is very strong, it will not be administered unless the citizens request it themselves. It is also heard that the bureau has compiled a simple explanation of the cause of dysentery and the mode of transmission, prevention and treatment, and is printing it for wide publicity to facilitate the prevention methods. Do not eat items that have been touched by flies and raw water and raw tea. Contact with dysentery patients should wash hands and do not use the clothes, bedding and utensils that have been used by the patients and have not been disinfected. It is especially important because dysentery is a gastrointestinal disease and bacteria are often attached to the feet of flies or in raw water, so things that have been touched by flies and raw water must not be eaten to avoid accidentally introducing dysentery bacteria into the stomach and causing dysentery.

Eighteen Arrested in Ling Runxiang Assassination Case 178

The bandits dripped blood on their hands before committing the crime and swore an oath. They used the excuse of performing a play on a wide stage to collect money. The detectives went to arrest them and captured them in one fell swoop.

Ling Runxiang, a supervisor of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, was shot and killed by thugs on the 28th of last month at the entrance of Dexingli, Peng Road. After the incident, Director Yuan paid great attention to the case and immediately issued an order to his subordinates to strictly investigate and arrest the perpetrators. After receiving the order, Captain Xu of the Investigation Team also instructed his staff to speed up the investigation and secretly offered a reward in order to solve the case as soon as possible. Now it is known that the principal culprit and suspects were arrested in the Guangwu Theater in Zhabei the day before yesterday. After being interrogated by Captain Lu one by one, they confessed in detail. They were escorted to the judicial section yesterday for review. The details of the arrest are explained in detail below.

Early Prevention: At the beginning of last month, when the Ling case had not yet occurred, Director Yuan repeatedly received secret reports that the reorganized faction and the confidants of Bai Chongxi and other rebels, the Guangdong brothers Ou Tian and Ou Chi, and the reactionaries such as Zhang Wei, Pan Qi, Zhang Xitang, and Ou Pei, were secretly lurking in Shanghai, colluding with local unemployed ruffians, and attempting to cause disturbances and disrupt the rear. Please order officials to arrest them quickly to curb the chaos. After receiving the report, Director Yuan considered the matter important and immediately ordered the Investigation Team to conduct a strict investigation in preparation for prevention.

Unemployed Loafers: After receiving the order, Captain Lu immediately informed his subordinates to find out the truth and report back within a limited time. After five days, the detectives reported back that the group was indeed hiding in Yuexiufang, Haining Road, Public Concession, and Dexingli, Peng Road, etc., and Pan Qi and Zhang Xitang were indeed famous unemployed loafers in Guangdong who had been wanted by Guangdong officials. Their reputation in the Hongkou area is quite bad.

Hearing the News and Taking Precautions: After receiving the reply, Director Yuan immediately secretly ordered Captain Lu to supervise the detectives to arrest them at the addresses together with the relevant patrol room to prevent them from escaping the net, and to conduct strict inspections of all books and letters in the residences of the criminals. When Captain Lu was preparing to start preparing, he suddenly received a report that the rebels had heard the news and were taking precautions, so it was inconvenient to act rashly. He then reported the situation to Director Yuan, who ordered him to slow down the time and wait for the rebels to organize themselves before annihilating them in one fell swoop.

Performing a Play to Collect Money: After receiving the order, Lu was preparing to continue the investigation. Unexpectedly, on July 28, Supervisor Ling Runxiang was assassinated. A few days later, an informant secretly reported that the mastermind and persons related to the case were Ou Zhaocheng (ie Ou Tian) and Zhang Borong (ie Zhang Xitang), etc. The criminals were now borrowing the Guangwu Hall Theater in Qiujiang Road, Zhabei, to perform a play to collect money. Please go and arrest them quickly, etc. Then Captain Lu reported the situation to the director, who ordered the arrest.

Eighteen Arrested: Captain Lu, together with detectives Zhang Guangsen, Qi Haitian, Wang Shifu, Wang Yaogao, Ju Chuan, Shan Bin, Ding Shunbao, Han Ruisheng, Lv Xingchun, Han Jingxiang, Wu Kezhong, Zhou Peisan, Liu Furong, Wu Zuorong, Chen Jiren, Liu Yongfu, He Haifa, and Liu Enyu, went to arrest them together with the third patrol team at about 9 pm on the same day. Ou Tian, Zhang Xitang, Luo Baoliang, Guo Cheng, Liu Xizhuang, Liang Wenhong, Luo Yu, Ou Tu, Mo Yang, Ji Jiacong, Liang Biao, He Yaoquan, Ou Chuntong, He Wei, Luo Xianling, Zheng Lan, Yong Tan Guoan, Feng Wen and other eighteen people were arrested on the spot.

Informant's Words: When Captain Lu led the team to arrest them, he was deeply worried that the group would flee after hearing the news, so he first mixed the informant into the theater to monitor them from the side, and then rushed in and arrested them one by one and took them back to the team for interrogation. According to the confession, several days before the Ling case occurred, Ou Chuntong, Zhang Xitang, Feng and He, Ying Pan Qi, Ou Chang, Ou Zhuo, and Luo Qingyun were drinking tea in the Guangdong Merchant Tea House on North Sichuan Road to plan the assassination of He Ling (ie Ling Runxiang).

Swearing an Oath by Dripping Blood: The first suggestion was that A Ling is now working in the Public Security Bureau. We all know his appearance and everything about the case. I am afraid that it will be detrimental to me. At that time, I decided to assassinate him to silence him. This matter was discussed for seven or eight days before it was finalized. Later, Pan Qi, Liu Zuoqing, etc. were afraid that their determination would not be firm, so they invited us to the San Yuan Temple on Dong Wuchang Road to chop off a chicken's head, drip blood to swear an oath, and write a master word as proof to prove that everyone was determined. At that time, Ou Chuntong, Zhang Xitang, Liu Zuoqing, Ou Zhuo, Pan Qi, Feng and He Ying, and Lu Ju, along with ten people whose names were unknown, totaling twenty people, burned incense, kowtowed, and swore an oath.

Zhang's Confession: Afterwards, the daily expenses were all subsidized by Pan Qi alone. The leaders of this matter were Ou Tian, Ou Chi, Ou Pei, Zhang Wei, Pan Qi and other five people. Then Zhang Borong (ie Xitang) confessed that all of this was planned by Pan Qi several times. At that time, He Ying brought Lu Ju and three people surnamed Luo to do it together. They brought one Type 38 revolver and two five-seed lotus root type revolvers. He Ying fired the gun and killed Ling. After questioning the other criminals, their confessions were evasive and ambiguous. After questioning them one by one, they immediately reported to the director and prepared a document to transfer the criminals to the judicial section for legal processing.

Yang Mingsheng Commits Suicide Due to Mental Illness 179

Acting abnormally and suffering from mental disorder, he jumped into the river and immediately drowned.

Yang Mingsheng, a 47-year-old man from Pudong Zhangjiangzha, used to work as a boat shaker in Baofeng Fish Shop, Wusong. Although he was a boatman, he was honest and upright, and his demeanor was always kind and amiable. Therefore, the superiors and subordinates of the shop were happy to associate with him, and the relationship was quite satisfactory. At lunchtime the day before yesterday, he suddenly changed his usual state, his actions changed suddenly, and he went to Baoshan alone to visit Zhao, who had been his colleague at the same time. Not long after, he went to the grave of a family outside the West Gate, and sat alone on top of the grave in the scorching sun. Passers-by suspected that he was ill, went up to call him, but he did not answer, and asked him, but he did not respond. Zhao then entered the city to inform Zhao, who went there to inquire, but the answers were not what he was asked. Zhao saw his strange behavior and incoherent words and knew that he had a mental disorder. He immediately accompanied him to Changchun Hotel, the site of the Song Commercial Association, and ordered him to sit and drink, while Zhao went to Baofeng to send a letter. Unexpectedly, Yang got up and went out after Zhao left, muttering to himself, "Someone is calling me to go with him," etc. As he spoke, he walked to the railway bridge on the west side of the Wusong Town Railway Station, took off his shoes, and jumped into the river and drowned without emerging. When his colleagues heard the news, they rushed to rescue him, but it was too late. Yesterday, the shop sent someone to report to his family and hired a boat to carry the body to Pudong for burial.
